/></a></td></tr></tbody></table><p><b>Aer Lingus</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\xcb\x8c</span><span title="/\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r/: &#39;are&#39; in &#39;bare&#39;">\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="/\xc5\x8b/: &#39;ng&#39; in &#39;sing&#39;">\xc5\x8b</span><span title="/\xc9\xa1/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">\xc9\xa1</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>, an <a href="/wiki/Anglicisation" title="Anglicisation">anglicisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text">aerloingeas</i></i><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> meaning "air fleet") is the <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a> of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>. Founded by the Irish government, it was privatised between 2006 and 2015 and it is now a wholly owned subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a> (IAG). The airline\'s head office is on the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cloghran,_Coolock" title="Cloghran, Coolock">Cloghran</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Dublin" title="County Dublin">County Dublin</a>.\n</p><p>Formed in 1936, Aer Lingus is a former member of the <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> airline alliance, which it left on 31 March 2007. After the takeover by IAG, it was expected that Aer Lingus would re-enter Oneworld, however, at a press briefing on 15 November 2017 the airline\'s then CEO Stephen Kavanagh stated that the airline has "no plans to join Oneworld".<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The airline has <a href="/wiki/Codeshare" class="mw-redirect" title="Codeshare">codeshares</a> with Oneworld, <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> and <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> members, as well as interline agreements with <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/JetBlue_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="JetBlue Airways">JetBlue Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>. Aer Lingus has a <a href="/wiki/Porter%27s_generic_strategies" title="Porter&#39;s generic strategies">hybrid business model</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> operating a mixed fare service<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> on its European routes and full service, two-class flights on transatlantic routes.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> owned over 29% of Aer Lingus stock and the Irish state owned over 25% before being bought out by IAG in 2015. The state had previously held an 85% shareholding until the Government\'s decision to float the company on the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Stock Exchange">Dublin</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London</a> stock exchanges on 2 October 2006. The principal group companies include Aer Lingus Limited, Aer Lingus Beachey Limited, Aer Lingus (Ireland) Limited and Dirnan Insurance Company Limited, all of which are wholly owned.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 26 May 2015, after months of negotiations on a possible IAG takeover, the Irish government agreed to sell its 25% stake in the company. Ryanair retained a 30% stake in Aer Lingus which it agreed to sell to IAG on 10 July 2015 for \xe2\x82\xac2.55 per share.<sup id="cite_ref-irishtimes.com_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irishtimes.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Martin-Tel_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-Tel-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In August 2015, Aer Lingus\' shareholders officially accepted IAG\'s takeover offer.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> IAG subsequently assumed control of Aer Lingus on 2 September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-IAGShare_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IAGShare-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Appointment_of_Christoph_Mueller_as_CEO"><span class="tocnumber">1.5.9</span> <span class="toctext">Appointment of Christoph Mueller as CEO</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16"><a href="#75th_anniversary"><span class="tocnumber">1.5.10</span> <span class="toctext">75th anniversary</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-17"><a href="#Third_Ryanair_takeover_bid_(2012)"><span class="tocnumber">1.5.11</span> <span class="toctext">Third Ryanair takeover bid (2012)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-18"><a href="#Virgin_Atlantic_wet-lease_agreement"><span class="tocnumber">1.5.12</span> <span class="toctext">Virgin Atlantic wet-lease agreement</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#Long-haul_expansion"><span class="tocnumber">1.5.13</span> <span class="toctext">Long-haul expansion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Change_of_CEO"><span class="tocnumber">1.5.14</span> <span class="toctext">Change of CEO</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21"><a href="#IAG_takeover_(2014/2015)"><span class="tocnumber">1.5.15</span> <span class="toctext">IAG takeover (2014/2015)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#COVID-19_(2020)"><span class="tocnumber">1.5.16</span> <span class="toctext">COVID-19 (2020)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Corporate_affairs"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Corporate affairs</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Ownership_and_structure"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ownership and structure</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-25"><a href="#Aer_Lingus_Cargo"><span class="tocnumber">2.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Aer Lingus Cargo</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-26"><a href="#Aer_Lingus_Regional"><span class="tocnumber">2.1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Aer Lingus Regional</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Business_trends"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Business trends</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Business_model"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Business model</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Head_office"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Head office</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Employee_relations"><span class="tocnumber">2.5</span> <span class="toctext">Employee relations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Sponsorships"><span class="tocnumber">2.6</span> <span class="toctext">Sponsorships</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Destinations"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Destinations</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Codeshare_agreements"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Codeshare agreements</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Fleet"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Fleet</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Current_fleet"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Current fleet</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Fleet_development"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Fleet development</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Historical_fleet"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Historical fleet</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Livery"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Livery</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Services"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Services</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#In-flight_services"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">In-flight services</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#Frequent-flyer_programme"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Frequent-flyer programme</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#Accidents_and_incidents"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Accidents and incidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Aer Lingus was founded on 15 April 1936, with a capital of \xc2\xa3100,000. Its first chairman was Se\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x93&#160;hUadhaigh.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Pending legislation for Government investment through a parent company, Aer Lingus was associated with Blackpool and West Coast Air Services which advanced the money for the first aircraft, and operated with Aer Lingus under the common title "Irish Sea Airways".<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iawa_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iawa-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Aer Lingus <a href="/wiki/Teoranta" class="mw-redirect" title="Teoranta">Teoranta</a> was registered as an airline on 22 May 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-EI_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The name <i>Aer Lingus</i> was proposed by Richard F O\'Connor, who was <a href="/wiki/County_Cork" title="County Cork">County Cork</a> Surveyor, as well as an aviation enthusiast.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_De_Havilland_DH-84_Dragon_2_EI-ABI_OTT_2013_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Aer_Lingus_De_Havilland_DH-84_Dragon_2_EI-ABI_OTT_2013_03.jpg/240px-Aer_Lingus_De_Havilland_DH-84_Dragon_2_EI-ABI_OTT_2013_03.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Aer_Lingus_De_Havilland_DH-84_Dragon_2_EI-ABI_OTT_2013_03.jpg/360px-Aer_Lingus_De_Havilland_DH-84_Dragon_2_EI-ABI_OTT_2013_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Aer_Lingus_De_Havilland_DH-84_Dragon_2_EI-ABI_OTT_2013_03.jpg/480px-Aer_Lingus_De_Havilland_DH-84_Dragon_2_EI-ABI_OTT_2013_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3400" data-file-height="1912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_De_Havilland_DH-84_Dragon_2_EI-ABI_OTT_2013_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A DH.84 Dragon, repainted in the livery of Aer Lingus\' original aircraft "Iolar".</div></div></div>\n<p>On 27 May 1936, five days after being registered as an airline, its first service began between <a href="/wiki/Casement_Aerodrome" title="Casement Aerodrome">Baldonnel Airfield</a> in Dublin and <a href="/wiki/Bristol_(Whitchurch)_Airport" title="Bristol (Whitchurch) Airport">Bristol (Whitchurch) Airport</a>, the United Kingdom, using a six-seater <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Dragon" title="De Havilland Dragon">de Havilland DH.84 Dragon</a> biplane (registration EI-ABI), named <i>Iolar</i> (Eagle).\n</p><p>Later that year, the airline acquired its second aircraft, a four-engined biplane <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Express" title="De Havilland Express">de Havilland DH.86 Express</a> named "\xc3\x89ire", with a capacity of 14 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-iawa_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iawa-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> This aircraft provided the first air link between Dublin and London by extending the Bristol service to <a href="/wiki/Croydon" title="Croydon">Croydon</a>. At the same time, the DH.84 Dragon was used to inaugurate an Aer Lingus service on the Dublin-Liverpool route.\n</p><p>The airline was established as the national carrier under the <a href="/wiki/Air_Navigation_and_Transport_Act" title="Air Navigation and Transport Act">Air Navigation and Transport Act</a> (1936).<sup id="cite_ref-EI_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In 1937, the Irish government created Aer Rianta (now called <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Airport Authority">Dublin Airport Authority</a>), a company to assume financial responsibility for the new airline and the entire country\'s civil aviation infrastructure. In April 1937, Aer Lingus became wholly owned by the Irish government via Aer Rianta.\n</p><p>The airline\'s first General Manager was Dr J.F. (Jeremiah known as \'Jerry\') Dempsey, a chartered accountant, who joined the company on secondment from Kennedy Crowley &amp; Co (predecessor to <a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>) as Company Secretary in 1936 (aged 30) and was appointed to the role of General Manager in 1937. He retired 30 years later in 1967 at the age of 60.\n</p><p>In 1938, a <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Dragon_Rapide" title="De Havilland Dragon Rapide">de Havilland DH.89 Dragon Rapide</a> replaced <i>Iolar</i>, and the company purchased a second DH.86B. Two <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Model_14_Super_Electra" title="Lockheed Model 14 Super Electra">Lockheed 14s</a> arrived in 1939, Aer Lingus\' first all-metal aircraft.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_DC-3_Manchester_1949.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Aer_Lingus_DC-3_Manchester_1949.jpg/220px-Aer_Lingus_DC-3_Manchester_1949.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Aer_Lingus_DC-3_Manchester_1949.jpg/330px-Aer_Lingus_DC-3_Manchester_1949.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Aer_Lingus_DC-3_Manchester_1949.jpg/440px-Aer_Lingus_DC-3_Manchester_1949.jpg 2x" data-file-width="794" data-file-height="419" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_DC-3_Manchester_1949.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Aer Lingus <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">Douglas DC-3</a> at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a> in 1948 wearing the first postwar livery.</div></div></div>\n<p>In January 1940, a new airport opened in the Dublin suburb of Collinstown and Aer Lingus moved its operations there. It purchased a new <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">DC-3</a> and inaugurated new services to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> and an internal service to <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon</a>. The airline\'s services were curtailed during World War II with the sole route being to Liverpool or <a href="/wiki/City_Airport_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="City Airport Manchester">Barton Aerodrome</a> Manchester depending on the fluctuating security situation.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_expansion">Post-war expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Post-war expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 9 November 1945, regular services were resumed with an inaugural flight to London. From this point Aer Lingus aircraft, initially mostly <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">Douglas DC-3s</a>, were painted in a silver and green livery. The airline introduced its first flight attendants.\n</p><p>In 1946, a new Anglo-Irish agreement gave Aer Lingus exclusive UK traffic rights from Ireland in exchange for a 40% holding by <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Airways_Corporation" title="British Overseas Airways Corporation">British Overseas Airways Corporation</a> (BOAC) and <a href="/wiki/British_European_Airways" title="British European Airways">British European Airways</a> (BEA). Because of Aer Lingus\' growth the airline bought seven new <a href="/wiki/Vickers_VC.1_Viking" title="Vickers VC.1 Viking">Vickers Viking</a> aircraft in 1947, however, these proved to be uneconomical and were soon sold.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bristol_170.31_EI-AFS_Aer_Lingus_Ringway_08.53_edited-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bristol_170.31_EI-AFS_Aer_Lingus_Ringway_08.53_edited-2.jpg/220px-Bristol_170.31_EI-AFS_Aer_Lingus_Ringway_08.53_edited-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bristol_170.31_EI-AFS_Aer_Lingus_Ringway_08.53_edited-2.jpg/330px-Bristol_170.31_EI-AFS_Aer_Lingus_Ringway_08.53_edited-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bristol_170.31_EI-AFS_Aer_Lingus_Ringway_08.53_edited-2.jpg/440px-Bristol_170.31_EI-AFS_Aer_Lingus_Ringway_08.53_edited-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1087" data-file-height="667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bristol_170.31_EI-AFS_Aer_Lingus_Ringway_08.53_edited-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Bristol_170_Freighter" class="mw-redirect" title="Bristol 170 Freighter">Bristol 170 Freighter</a> at Manchester Airport in 1953.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1947, Aerl\xc3\xadnte \xc3\x89ireann came into existence to operate <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_flight" title="Transatlantic flight">transatlantic flights</a> to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> from Ireland. The airline ordered five new <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_L-749_Constellation" title="Lockheed L-749 Constellation">Lockheed L-749 Constellations</a>, but a change of government and a financial crisis prevented the service from starting. <a href="/wiki/John_A_Costello" class="mw-redirect" title="John A Costello">John A Costello</a>, the incoming <a href="/wiki/Fine_Gael" title="Fine Gael">Fine Gael</a> <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> (Prime Minister), was not a keen supporter of air travel and thought that flying the Atlantic was too grandiose a scheme for a small airline from a small country like Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-Garvin_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garvin-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_Viscount_808_Manchester_1963.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Aer_Lingus_Viscount_808_Manchester_1963.jpg/220px-Aer_Lingus_Viscount_808_Manchester_1963.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Aer_Lingus_Viscount_808_Manchester_1963.jpg/330px-Aer_Lingus_Viscount_808_Manchester_1963.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Aer_Lingus_Viscount_808_Manchester_1963.jpg/440px-Aer_Lingus_Viscount_808_Manchester_1963.jpg 2x" data-file-width="752" data-file-height="416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_Viscount_808_Manchester_1963.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> 808 in "green top" livery at Manchester Airport in 1963.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the late 1940s and early 1950s, Aer Lingus introduced routes to <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airport" title="Brussels Airport">Brussels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Airport">Amsterdam</a> via <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester</a> and to Rome. Because of the expanding route structure, the airline became one of the early purchasers of <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> 700s in 1951, which were placed in service in April 1954. In 1952, the airline expanded its all-freight services and acquired a small fleet of <a href="/wiki/Bristol_170_Freighter" class="mw-redirect" title="Bristol 170 Freighter">Bristol 170 Freighters</a>, which remained in service until 1957.\n</p><p>Prof. <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Lynch_(economist)" title="Patrick Lynch (economist)">Patrick Lynch</a> was appointed the chairman of Aer Lingus and <a href="/wiki/Aer_Rianta" class="mw-redirect" title="Aer Rianta">Aer Rianta</a> in 1954<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and served in the position until 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 1956, Aer Lingus introduced a new, green-top livery with a white lightning flash down the windows and the Irish flag displayed on the fin.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_transatlantic_service">First transatlantic service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: First transatlantic service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_720-048_EI-ALA_Aer_Lingus_1965.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Boeing_720-048_EI-ALA_Aer_Lingus_1965.jpg/220px-Boeing_720-048_EI-ALA_Aer_Lingus_1965.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Boeing_720-048_EI-ALA_Aer_Lingus_1965.jpg/330px-Boeing_720-048_EI-ALA_Aer_Lingus_1965.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Boeing_720-048_EI-ALA_Aer_Lingus_1965.jpg/440px-Boeing_720-048_EI-ALA_Aer_Lingus_1965.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1680" data-file-height="1040" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_720-048_EI-ALA_Aer_Lingus_1965.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Boeing_720" title="Boeing 720">Boeing 720</a> in Aer Lingus-Irish International livery in 1965.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 28 April 1958, Aerl\xc3\xadnte \xc3\x89ireann operated its first transatlantic service from <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon</a> to New York.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In 1960, Aerl\xc3\xadnte \xc3\x89ireann was renamed Aer Lingus.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Aer Lingus bought seven <a href="/wiki/Fokker_F27_Friendship" title="Fokker F27 Friendship">Fokker F27 Friendships</a>, which were delivered between November 1958 and May 1959. These were used in short-haul services to the UK, gradually replacing the Dakotas, until Aer Lingus replaced them in 1966 with secondhand Viscount 800s.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airline entered the jet age on 14 December 1960 when it received three <a href="/wiki/Boeing_720" title="Boeing 720">Boeing 720</a> for use on the New York route and the newest Aer Lingus destination <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>.\n</p><p>In 1963, Aer Lingus added <a href="/wiki/Aviation_Traders_Carvair" title="Aviation Traders Carvair">Aviation Traders Carvairs</a> to the fleet. These aircraft could transport five cars which were loaded into the fuselage through the nose of the aircraft. The Carvair proved to be uneconomical for the airline partly due to the rise of <a href="/wiki/Roll-on/roll-off" title="Roll-on/roll-off">auto ferry services</a>, and the aircraft were used for freight services until disposed of.\n</p><p>The Boeing 720s proved to be a success for the airline on the transatlantic routes. To supplement these, Aer Lingus took delivery of its first larger Boeing 707 in 1964, and the type continued to serve the airline until 1986.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jet_aircraft">Jet aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Jet aircraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_Fokker_Friendship_Manchester_1965.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Aer_Lingus_Fokker_Friendship_Manchester_1965.jpg/220px-Aer_Lingus_Fokker_Friendship_Manchester_1965.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Aer_Lingus_Fokker_Friendship_Manchester_1965.jpg/330px-Aer_Lingus_Fokker_Friendship_Manchester_1965.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Aer_Lingus_Fokker_Friendship_Manchester_1965.jpg/440px-Aer_Lingus_Fokker_Friendship_Manchester_1965.jpg 2x" data-file-width="752" data-file-height="416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_Fokker_Friendship_Manchester_1965.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Fokker_F27" class="mw-redirect" title="Fokker F27">Fokker F27</a> Friendship at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a> in 1965. The F27 was used on short-haul services between 1958 and 1966.</div></div></div>\n<p>Conversion of the European fleet to jet equipment began in 1965 when the <a href="/wiki/BAC_One-Eleven" title="BAC One-Eleven">BAC One-Eleven</a> started services on continental Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The airline adopted a new livery in the same year, with a large green <a href="/wiki/Shamrock_(Irish_symbol)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shamrock (Irish symbol)">shamrock</a> on the fin.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 1966, the remainder of the company\'s shares held by <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Airport Authority">Aer Rianta</a> were transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Finance_(Ireland)" title="Minister for Finance (Ireland)">Minister for Finance</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carvair_and_ambassador_at_bristol_airport_1965_arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Carvair_and_ambassador_at_bristol_airport_1965_arp.jpg/220px-Carvair_and_ambassador_at_bristol_airport_1965_arp.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Carvair_and_ambassador_at_bristol_airport_1965_arp.jpg/330px-Carvair_and_ambassador_at_bristol_airport_1965_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Carvair_and_ambassador_at_bristol_airport_1965_arp.jpg/440px-Carvair_and_ambassador_at_bristol_airport_1965_arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2922" data-file-height="1798" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carvair_and_ambassador_at_bristol_airport_1965_arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Aviation_Traders_Carvair" title="Aviation Traders Carvair">Aviation Traders Carvair</a> that was used as a vehicle freighter is seen loading a car at <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Airport" title="Bristol Airport">Bristol Airport</a> in 1964.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1966, the company added routes to <a href="/wiki/Montr%C3%A9al-Pierre_Elliott_Trudeau_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Montr\xc3\xa9al-Pierre Elliott Trudeau International Airport">Montreal</a> and <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O&#39;Hare International Airport">Chicago</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 1968, flights from <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, to New York City started, however, it was soon suspended due to the beginning of <a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">the Troubles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Aer Lingus introduced <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737s</a> to its fleet in 1969 to cope with the high demand for flights between Dublin and London.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Later, Aer Lingus extended the 737 flights to all of its European networks.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1967, after 30 years of service, General Manager Dr J.F. Dempsey signed the contract for the airline\'s first two <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> aircraft before he retired later that year.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s_to_present">1970s to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1970s to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_BAC_1-11_at_Zurich_-_July_1975.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Aer_Lingus_BAC_1-11_at_Zurich_-_July_1975.jpg/220px-Aer_Lingus_BAC_1-11_at_Zurich_-_July_1975.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Aer_Lingus_BAC_1-11_at_Zurich_-_July_1975.jpg/330px-Aer_Lingus_BAC_1-11_at_Zurich_-_July_1975.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Aer_Lingus_BAC_1-11_at_Zurich_-_July_1975.jpg/440px-Aer_Lingus_BAC_1-11_at_Zurich_-_July_1975.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_BAC_1-11_at_Zurich_-_July_1975.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A BAC One-Eleven in the old livery at <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Airport" title="Zurich Airport">Zurich Airport</a>, Switzerland in 1975.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 6 March 1971, Aer Lingus took delivery of the first of two <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747s</a> for use on the transatlantic routes.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The company later purchased a third for its fleet but quickly offered it for lease because it was not initially profitable for the company to fly 747s across the Atlantic. In 1974, Aer Lingus unveiled a new livery which eliminated the word <i>International</i> and/or <i>Irish</i> from the fuselage titles. The livery included two colours of blue and one green, plus the white shamrock on the fin.\n</p><p>In 1977, Aer Lingus recruited its first female pilot, <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%A1inne_Cronin" title="Gr\xc3\xa1inne Cronin">Gr\xc3\xa1inne Cronin</a> \xe2\x80\x93 the airline was the second in Europe (after <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">SAS</a>) to introduce female pilots.<sup id="cite_ref-Murray_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murray-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 1979, Aer Lingus became the first European airline other than <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a> to be used by <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a>, when he flew aboard a specially modified Boeing 747 (EI-ASI or St. Patrick) from Rome to Dublin and later from Shannon to <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>. In the early 1980s, the 707s were phased out.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_(EI-CFD),_Dublin,_February_1993.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Aer_Lingus_%28EI-CFD%29%2C_Dublin%2C_February_1993.jpg/220px-Aer_Lingus_%28EI-CFD%29%2C_Dublin%2C_February_1993.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Aer_Lingus_%28EI-CFD%29%2C_Dublin%2C_February_1993.jpg/330px-Aer_Lingus_%28EI-CFD%29%2C_Dublin%2C_February_1993.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Aer_Lingus_%28EI-CFD%29%2C_Dublin%2C_February_1993.jpg/440px-Aer_Lingus_%28EI-CFD%29%2C_Dublin%2C_February_1993.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3407" data-file-height="2279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_(EI-CFD),_Dublin,_February_1993.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Aer Lingus Commuter <a href="/wiki/Saab_340" title="Saab 340">Saab 340</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin Airport</a> in 1993.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1984, the airline formed a fully owned subsidiary, Aer Lingus Commuter, so that Aer Lingus could fly to larger cities in Ireland and Britain whose flying time from Dublin did not require jet aircraft. These services employed five of the Belfast-built <a href="/wiki/Short_360" title="Short 360">Short 360</a> after conducting a trial with the <a href="/wiki/Short_330" title="Short 330">Short 330</a>. Around this time Aer Lingus purchased a majority shareholding in the <a href="/wiki/Cargo_airline" title="Cargo airline">cargo airline</a> <a href="/wiki/Aer_Turas" title="Aer Turas">Aer Turas</a>, owner of some <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-8" title="Douglas DC-8">DC-8</a> freighter jets.\n</p><p>Between 1987 and 1989, new <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737s</a> arrived to replace the older ones, and six <a href="/wiki/Fokker_50" title="Fokker 50">Fokker 50s</a> were added to the <i>Commuter</i> fleet. During 1990, after the passage of the deregulation act for the airline industry in Ireland, Aer Lingus reconsidered its operational policies. It retired the BAC One-Elevens and replaced them with five new 737s. In 1991, four <a href="/wiki/Saab_340" title="Saab 340">Saab 340</a>Bs arrived at the commuter division to replace the <a href="/wiki/Short_360" title="Short 360">Short 360</a> aircraft. By 1992, Aer Lingus\'s entire original 737-200 fleet had been replaced and it was now the first carrier in the world operating all three versions of the second-generation 737. These were the \xe2\x88\x92300, \xe2\x88\x92400 and \xe2\x88\x92500 series, although the \xe2\x88\x92300 did not stay long in Aer Lingus service.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Airbus_operations">Airbus operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Airbus operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerlingus.a321-200.ei-cpe.arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Aerlingus.a321-200.ei-cpe.arp.jpg/220px-Aerlingus.a321-200.ei-cpe.arp.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Aerlingus.a321-200.ei-cpe.arp.jpg/330px-Aerlingus.a321-200.ei-cpe.arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Aerlingus.a321-200.ei-cpe.arp.jpg/440px-Aerlingus.a321-200.ei-cpe.arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2741" data-file-height="1749" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerlingus.a321-200.ei-cpe.arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a> landing at <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a> in 2007.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1994, Aer Lingus started direct services between Dublin and the United States using the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330</a> and in May of that year, Aer Lingus operated the first A330-300 <a href="/wiki/ETOPS" title="ETOPS">ETOPS</a> service over the North Atlantic. This led to the phasing out of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> and the briefly operated <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a>-300ER. On 2 October 1995, the Boeing 747 service ceased operations after twenty-five years of service. By that time, over eight million people had travelled across the Atlantic in Aer Lingus Boeing 747s. The late 1990s saw Aer Lingus return to <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> with service to New York via Shannon.  It also added <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Liberty International Airport</a> as a destination, but discontinued these flights in 2001.\n</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> short-haul aircraft arrived in 1998 in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">A321</a>, initially to mainly operate the Dublin-Heathrow route. Six were delivered in 1998 and 1999 and three of these continue in service today. The first <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">A320</a> was delivered in 2000, with three more added to the fleet by 2001.\n</p><p>On 1 February 2001, Aer Lingus Commuter merged back into the mainline operation. The business was severely affected by the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">11 September attacks</a>.  In response, the airline cut staff numbers and destinations and reduced its fleet.  As a result, it weathered the storm and returned to profit, largely through lowering the airline\'s cost base, updating the fleet with modern Airbus equipment and developing new routes to mainland European destinations. Aer Lingus had previously largely neglected mainland Europe in favour of US and British destinations.  It positioned itself as competition to the European <a href="/wiki/No_frills" title="No frills">no-frills</a> airlines while offering intercontinental flights, phased-out Business class travel for short-haul flights, but retained cargo services on a small number of routes.\n</p><p>A large order for A320 aircraft saw deliveries commencing in 2004 and continuing to 2011. The delivery of these aircraft allowed the withdrawal of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a>.  On 29 October 2005, Aer Lingus withdrew its last two 737 aircraft from service, marking the end of Boeing aircraft at Aer Lingus, and the beginning of an all-Airbus fleet.\n</p><p>On 27 October 2005, Aer Lingus announced its first scheduled service to Asia from March 2006 as <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai International Airport</a> in the United Arab Emirates, where Chief Executive <a href="/wiki/Dermot_Mannion" title="Dermot Mannion">Dermot Mannion</a> was based when at <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-privatise_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-privatise-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Despite the Aer Lingus press release describing it as the first long-haul service outside the United States, there had in fact been a previous service to <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> from 1966 to 1979. The <a href="/wiki/Great_circle" title="Great circle">great circle</a> distance of 5,926 kilometres (3,682&#160;mi) is comparable to the service to Chicago. At the same time, Mannion linked the funding of new long-haul aircraft to replace the A330 fleet with the privatisation of the airline.<sup id="cite_ref-ReplaceA330_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReplaceA330-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The Dubai service ceased in March 2008 as the airline sought to increase its market share in the newly liberalised transatlantic market.\n</p><p>On 6 June 2007, Aer Lingus strengthened its relationship with the European manufacturer by ordering six of the new A350-900 and six A330-300. These were used to expand long-haul operations as well as replace three older models. Deliveries of the A330 began in February 2009. In, 2011 Aer Lingus switched their remaining three A330 orders to A350-900s, with delivery no sooner than 2017. The A350 orders were subsequently assumed by IAG in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-fleet_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fleet-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IAG_Capital_Markets_Day_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IAG_Capital_Markets_Day-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flotation">Flotation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Flotation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wing_0587.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Wing_0587.JPG/220px-Wing_0587.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Wing_0587.JPG/330px-Wing_0587.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Wing_0587.JPG/440px-Wing_0587.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wing_0587.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Aer Lingus logo painted on an Airbus A330 <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device" title="Wingtip device">winglet</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In preparation for the commercial flotation of Aer Lingus on the Dublin stock market, the Irish government agreed to abolish the <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport#Shannon_stopover" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon Stopover</a> from the end of 2006 in stages.\n</p><p>The company began conditional (or "grey-market") share dealings on 27 September 2006 and was formally admitted to the Official Lists of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Stock Exchange">Irish Stock Exchange</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> on 2 October 2006. At the time of the flotation, the Irish government maintained a 28% shareholding, while employees held 15%. The stock IPO offer price was E2.20.<sup id="cite_ref-SharePrice_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SharePrice-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hennessy_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hennessy-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Aer Lingus withdrew from the Oneworld airline alliance on 31 March 2007, instead, entering into bilateral agreements with airlines including <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>. Aer Lingus explained the move stating the carrier was repositioning as a low-cost carrier, which did not fit with Oneworld\'s pitch to the premium international frequent flyer.\n</p><p>On 6 February 2007, however, the airline announced its intention to form a new alliance with <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a>. This new alliance was to act as a weblink between the two airlines, enabling Aer Lingus customers to book JetBlue destinations from the Aer Lingus website. In 2008, it also announced an alliance with <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> for connecting services within the US.\n</p><p>With the flotation of Aer Lingus on the stock exchange, Aer Lingus had planned to expand its route network, but this was put on hold due to the economic situation.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="First_Ryanair_takeover_bid_.282006.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Ryanair_takeover_bid_(2006)">First Ryanair takeover bid (2006)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: First Ryanair takeover bid (2006)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 5 October 2006, Ryanair launched a bid to buy Aer Lingus. Ryanair CEO <a href="/wiki/Michael_O%27Leary_(Ryanair)" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael O&#39;Leary (Ryanair)">Michael O\'Leary</a> said the move was a "unique opportunity" to form an Irish airline. The "new" airline would carry over 50&#160;million passengers a year. Ryanair said it had bought a 16% stake in Aer Lingus and was offering \xe2\x82\xac2.80 for the remaining shares, a premium over the \xe2\x82\xac2.20 the shares were trading for. The firm was trading at \xe2\x82\xac1.13bn but Ryanair\'s offer valued it at \xe2\x82\xac1.48bn.<sup id="cite_ref-Reject_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reject-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> On the same day Aer Lingus rejected Ryanair\'s takeover bid.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On 5 October 2006, Ryanair confirmed it had raised its stake to 19.2%, and said it had no problem in the Irish Government keeping its 28.3%.  <i><a href="/wiki/The_Irish_Times" title="The Irish Times">The Irish Times</a></i> reported that the Government would possibly seek judgement from the courts, and referral to competition authorities in Dublin \xe2\x80\x93 although this would be automatic under European regulation, as the combined group would control 78% of the Dublin \xe2\x80\x93 London passenger air traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-Lifts_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lifts-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 29 November 2006, Ryanair confirmed it had taken its stake to 26.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-Elderfield_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elderfield-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 December 2006, Ryanair announced it was withdrawing its bid for Aer Lingus, with the intent of pursuing another bid soon after the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> finishes investigating the bid. The EC has been concerned that the takeover would reduce consumer choice and increase fares.<sup id="cite_ref-CNBC_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNBC-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 June 2007, the European Commission announced its decision to block the bid on competition grounds saying the two airlines controlled more than 80% of all European flights to and from Dublin Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-Blocked_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blocked-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cross_border_expansion">Cross border expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cross border expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 7 August 2007, the airline announced that it would establish its first base outside the Republic of Ireland at <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. Services from Belfast International commenced in December 2007. As of July&#160;2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the airline had three <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320</a> aircraft based at the airport, serving eleven European destinations. Significantly, this move restored the Belfast International to <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a> link and Aer Lingus cooperated with its codeshare partner British Airways on this route to connect with BA\'s network at Heathrow. To do so, the airline discontinued its <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon</a>-Heathrow service, a move that generated political controversy in the west of Ireland, particularly as the Shannon-London route was still profitable. The airline predicted that this move would add one million additional passengers annually.<sup id="cite_ref-Appeals_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Appeals-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The Shannon to <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a> service has since been reinstated.\n</p><p>After five years at Belfast International Airport, Aer Lingus announced on 19 July 2012 that it would be moving its operations to <a href="/wiki/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport" title="George Best Belfast City Airport">George Best Belfast City Airport</a>. The airline transferred its Belfast \xe2\x80\x93 London Heathrow flights to there, and also announced the operation of a thrice-daily London Gatwick service (no longer operated), and on 31 March 2013, launched services to Faro and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="M\xc3\xa1laga">M\xc3\xa1laga</a>. Aer Lingus based 2 aircraft in Belfast City Airport for the Winter 2012\xe2\x80\x932013 season and a third aircraft arrived for the Summer 2013 season.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_Skies">Open Skies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Open Skies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 22 March 2007, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/EU%E2%80%93US_Open_Skies_Agreement" title="EU\xe2\x80\x93US Open Skies Agreement">EU\xe2\x80\x93US Open Skies Agreement</a>, Aer Lingus announced three new long-haul services to the United States. From Autumn 2007, Aer Lingus commenced direct flights to <a href="/wiki/Orlando_International_Airport" title="Orlando International Airport">Orlando</a>, San Francisco and Washington, D.C.-<a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">Dulles</a>, facilitated by the arrival of two new Airbus A330 aircraft in May 2007. The airline also serves <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> (<a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Logan International Airport</a>), Chicago (<a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O&#39;Hare International Airport">O\'Hare International Airport</a>), and New York (<a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">JFK Airport</a>). Aer Lingus ended its Middle-Eastern Route to <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai</a> in March 2008 and ended its Los Angeles route in November 2008. The <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington</a> and the San Francisco routes were discontinued as of 24&#160;October&#160;2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>. Services from Washington, D.C. resumed on 28 March 2010 when the airline began flights from Washington D.C. to <a href="/wiki/Madrid-Barajas_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Madrid-Barajas Airport">Madrid</a>, Spain in a joint venture with United Airlines. The airline terminated this route on 30 October 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Hancock_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hancock-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Services from San Francisco have since resumed on 2 April 2014. New Route: Dublin-Washington Aer Lingus has given details of its Summer 2015 schedule which includes the introduction of a new, four times weekly summer service from Dublin to Washington-Dulles starting May 2015.  The Dublin-Los Angeles route was reintroduced on 4 May 2016.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_of_global_financial_crisis">Effects of global financial crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Effects of global financial crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After reporting losses of \xe2\x82\xac22&#160;million for the first half of the year, in October 2008, Aer Lingus announced a \xe2\x82\xac74&#160;million cost-saving plan.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> This plan included cutting up to 1,500 jobs, scaled back ground operations at the Cork airport, and outsourced all ground staff at the Dublin airport.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> This met with a largely negative response particularly from trade unions.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2008, Aer Lingus announced that the Shannon \xe2\x80\x93 Heathrow service would resume from 29 March 2009 following new arrangements with the trade unions on staff costs and the Shannon Airport Authority on airport charges.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> However at the end of June 2009 the company had accumulated losses of \xe2\x82\xac93&#160;million and Chairman Colm Barrington confirmed this situation could not continue.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In October 2009, newly appointed Chief Executive Christoph Mueller announced a radical cost-cutting plan that would lead to the loss of 676 jobs at the company and see pay and pension reductions for those being retained. The total plan aimed to achieve savings of \xe2\x82\xac97&#160;million between then and 2011. As a 6-week consultation process began, Mueller refused to rule out further cuts in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Second_Ryanair_takeover_bid_.282008.2F2009.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Ryanair_takeover_bid_(2008/2009)">Second Ryanair takeover bid (2008/2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Second Ryanair takeover bid (2008/2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_(EI-BDY),_Dublin,_July_1992_(01).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Aer_Lingus_%28EI-BDY%29%2C_Dublin%2C_July_1992_%2801%29.jpg/220px-Aer_Lingus_%28EI-BDY%29%2C_Dublin%2C_July_1992_%2801%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Aer_Lingus_%28EI-BDY%29%2C_Dublin%2C_July_1992_%2801%29.jpg/330px-Aer_Lingus_%28EI-BDY%29%2C_Dublin%2C_July_1992_%2801%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Aer_Lingus_%28EI-BDY%29%2C_Dublin%2C_July_1992_%2801%29.jpg/440px-Aer_Lingus_%28EI-BDY%29%2C_Dublin%2C_July_1992_%2801%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3407" data-file-height="2279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_(EI-BDY),_Dublin,_July_1992_(01).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Aer Lingus <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-200">Boeing 737-200</a> and a <a href="/wiki/BAC_One-Eleven" title="BAC One-Eleven">BAC One-Eleven</a> of rival airline <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> at Dublin Airport in 1992.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 1 December 2008, Ryanair launched a second takeover bid of Aer Lingus, making an all-cash offer of <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\xe2\x82\xac</a>748&#160;million (<a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">\xc2\xa3</a>619mil; US$950mil). The \xe2\x82\xac1.40 offer was a 28% premium on the average closing price of Aer Lingus stock during the 30 days to 28 November 28 (\xe2\x82\xac1.09), but half what Ryanair had offered in 2006. Ryanair said, "Aer Lingus, as a small, stand-alone, regional airline has been marginalised and bypassed as most other EU flag carriers consolidate." The two airlines would operate separately and Ryanair claimed that it would double the Aer Lingus short-haul fleet from 33 to 66 and create 1,000 new jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-08reject_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-08reject-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Michaels_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Michaels-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The Aer Lingus Board rejected the offer and advised its <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">shareholders</a> to take no action.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The offer was eventually rejected by a majority of the other shareholders. It was the second failed attempt by Michael O\'Leary to take over the national flag carrier. Ryanair initially left the offer open to Aer Lingus until it withdrew the bid on 28 January 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The Irish Government slammed O\'Leary\'s offer as "undervaluing the airline" and stated that a Ryanair takeover would have a "significant negative impact" on competition in the industry and on the Irish consumer.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair repeatedly stated that another bid was unlikely,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> but it kept a stake in Aer Lingus, prompting an investigation by competition regulators in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2009, Aer Lingus re-branded its <i>Premier Class</i> to the new <i>Business Class</i>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gatwick_base">Gatwick base</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Gatwick base">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_Airbus_A319-100_(EI-EPT)_departs_London_Heathrow_Airport,_England,_on_2ndJuly2014_arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Aer_Lingus_Airbus_A319-100_%28EI-EPT%29_departs_London_Heathrow_Airport%2C_England%2C_on_2ndJuly2014_arp.jpg/220px-Aer_Lingus_Airbus_A319-100_%28EI-EPT%29_departs_London_Heathrow_Airport%2C_England%2C_on_2ndJuly2014_arp.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Aer_Lingus_Airbus_A319-100_%28EI-EPT%29_departs_London_Heathrow_Airport%2C_England%2C_on_2ndJuly2014_arp.jpg/330px-Aer_Lingus_Airbus_A319-100_%28EI-EPT%29_departs_London_Heathrow_Airport%2C_England%2C_on_2ndJuly2014_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Aer_Lingus_Airbus_A319-100_%28EI-EPT%29_departs_London_Heathrow_Airport%2C_England%2C_on_2ndJuly2014_arp.jpg/440px-Aer_Lingus_Airbus_A319-100_%28EI-EPT%29_departs_London_Heathrow_Airport%2C_England%2C_on_2ndJuly2014_arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2031" data-file-height="1416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_Airbus_A319-100_(EI-EPT)_departs_London_Heathrow_Airport,_England,_on_2ndJuly2014_arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Aer Lingus <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319</a>-100 departs London-Heathrow in 2014.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer.lingus.a320-200.ei-den.arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Aer.lingus.a320-200.ei-den.arp.jpg/220px-Aer.lingus.a320-200.ei-den.arp.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Aer.lingus.a320-200.ei-den.arp.jpg/330px-Aer.lingus.a320-200.ei-den.arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Aer.lingus.a320-200.ei-den.arp.jpg/440px-Aer.lingus.a320-200.ei-den.arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1992" data-file-height="1316" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer.lingus.a320-200.ei-den.arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aer Lingus Airbus A320-200 lands at London Heathrow Airport, England.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 19 December 2008, Aer Lingus announced that it would open a base at <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a>. Four aircraft were based there beginning April 2009, serving eight destinations that included Dublin, Faro, Knock, M\xc3\xa1laga, Munich, Nice, Vienna and Z\xc3\xbcrich. CEO Dermot Mannion also said the company expects to increase the number of aircraft based at Gatwick to eight within 12 months.<sup id="cite_ref-Gatwick_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gatwick-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 6&#160;June&#160;2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the airline based an additional A320 aircraft at Gatwick, bringing the total number to five and making Gatwick its biggest base outside Ireland. This resulted in six new routes to Bucharest, Eindhoven, Lanzarote, Tenerife, Vilnius and Warsaw which commenced in late October 2009. The Gatwick to Nice route was suspended for the winter months.\n</p><p>On 8 January 2010, due to the weak demand in air travel, Aer Lingus announced that it was to reduce the number of aircraft based at Gatwick from five to three. The three remaining aircraft were to operate the carrier\'s services to Dublin, Knock and M\xc3\xa1laga as well as a new route to Cork.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2011, Aer Lingus announced a new daily service from Gatwick to Shannon starting at the end of March. The service has since been suspended.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The service to M\xc3\xa1laga was suspended in January 2012 and the base closed in 2015.\n</p><p>The Gatwick to Cork route ended 27 October 2012. A new service from Gatwick to Belfast City Airport started on 28 October, operating three times per day, and follows the airline\'s move from Belfast-International Airport to Belfast City Airport. That service was suspended on 27 April 2016.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Appointment_of_Christoph_Mueller_as_CEO">Appointment of Christoph Mueller as CEO</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Appointment of Christoph Mueller as CEO">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 6 April 2009, CEO <a href="/wiki/Dermot_Mannion" title="Dermot Mannion">Dermot Mannion</a> announced his resignation from the airline after four years as Chief Executive.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> He was replaced by German-born <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Mueller" title="Christoph Mueller">Christoph M\xc3\xbcller</a> (alternative spelling "Mueller"), former head of <a href="/wiki/TUI_Travel" title="TUI Travel">TUI Travel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sabena" title="Sabena">Sabena</a>, who joined Aer Lingus on 1 October 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Mueller_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mueller-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 2 December 2009, Aer Lingus announced that talks with its unions had broken down. As a result, the board voted to reduce capacity, and with it associated jobs, as a response. According to Mueller, concessions offered by unions were of a short-term nature, and the airline was asked for high compensation in return. Aer Lingus did not identify the routes or jobs to be cut, but they would most likely "commence immediately and will be compulsory," according to Mueller.<sup id="cite_ref-Axe_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Axe-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\nAs of April&#160;2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> all employees\' groups had passed votes on the acceptance of the \'Greenfield\' cost-cutting plans which were expected to save \xe2\x82\xac57M annually. Once implemented the second phase of cost-cutting was to commence which aimed to save \xe2\x82\xac40M annually by reducing \'back office staff\' numbers by up to 40% according to the CEO.\n</p><p>Mueller indicated that Aer Lingus intended to reposition itself again, moving away from head-to-head competition with <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> in the low-cost sector to a more hybrid model with a stronger emphasis on service. As part of this move, Aer Lingus entered talks to join an airline alliance again, having left Oneworld in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Alliance2010_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alliance2010-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Aer Lingus announced on 15 June 2010 that it would suspend services from <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon</a> to <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Boston</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York (JFK)</a> for 11 weeks beginning January 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="75th_anniversary">75th anniversary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 75th anniversary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Aer Lingus celebrated its 75th anniversary in 2011. On 26 March, the company presented its latest aircraft which has been painted in the 1960s <a href="/wiki/Livery" title="Livery">livery</a> and the crew was wearing a selection of historical uniforms.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Third_Ryanair_takeover_bid_.282012.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_Ryanair_takeover_bid_(2012)">Third Ryanair takeover bid (2012)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Third Ryanair takeover bid (2012)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 19 June 2012, Ryanair announced its intention to launch another bid to take over Aer Lingus, at \xe2\x82\xac1.30 per share, for a total of \xe2\x82\xac694 million.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Ryanair expressed the hope that the competition authorities would not block this attempt, pointing to the recent takeovers of <a href="/wiki/British_Midland_International" title="British Midland International">bmi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a> by <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a> (IAG) (parent company of <a href="/wiki/Iberia" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberia">Iberia</a> and British Airways) and <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><br />\nOn 20 June 2012, Aer Lingus issued a press release stating that having reviewed Ryanair\'s proposed offer, the company board rejected it and advised the company\'s shareholders not to take any action concerning it. The statement pointed out that any offer from Ryanair was unlikely to be capable of completion due to, firstly, the EU Commission\'s 2007 decision to block the airline\'s bid for Aer Lingus at the time, and, secondly, the <a href="/wiki/Competition_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Competition Commission (United Kingdom)">UK Competition Commission\'s</a> ongoing investigation of Ryanair\'s minority stake in Aer Lingus. Furthermore, the press release stated that the Aer Lingus board believed that Ryanair\'s offer undervalued Aer Lingus, considering the airline\'s profitability and balance sheet, including cash reserves over \xe2\x82\xac1 billion (as of 31&#160;March&#160;2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 February 2013, the European Commission blocked the third attempt by Ryanair to take over Aer Lingus, stating that the merger would have damaged consumers\' choice and resulted in increased fares.<sup id="cite_ref-Third_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Third-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Virgin_Atlantic_wet-lease_agreement">Virgin Atlantic wet-lease agreement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Virgin Atlantic wet-lease agreement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic_Little_Red" title="Virgin Atlantic Little Red">Virgin Atlantic Little Red</a></div>\n<p>In December 2012, following the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/British_Midland_International" title="British Midland International">British Midland International</a> by British Airways, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a> was awarded slots to fly domestic routes in the UK from Heathrow Airport, ending the monopoly on these services that BA had held since its successful takeover. Aer Lingus supplied on a <a href="/wiki/Wet_lease" class="mw-redirect" title="Wet lease">wet lease</a> agreement four Airbus A320-214 aircraft (painted in Virgin\'s colours but under Irish registration<sup id="cite_ref-fleet_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fleet-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>) as well as crew for these services, which operated from London Heathrow to Aberdeen, Edinburgh and Manchester. Services began on 31 March 2013 to Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> This wet-lease agreement ended in September 2015, as Virgin Atlantic cancelled its domestic services.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Long-haul_expansion">Long-haul expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Long-haul expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In July 2013, expansion into North America was announced launching in 2014; including a direct service from Dublin to <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_International_Airport" title="San Francisco International Airport">San Francisco</a> five times weekly and a daily service from Dublin to Toronto to be operated by <a href="/wiki/Air_Contractors" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Contractors">Air Contractors</a> with <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757s</a> on behalf of the airline. It was also announced that transatlantic services from Shannon to Boston and New York would operate daily all year round from January 2014 to Boston and from March 2014 to New York\'s <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a>; however, the airline would lease Boeing 757 aircraft from Air Contractors to operate these routes, rather than using its Airbus A330 aircraft as it had done before.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Also, the service to Washington Dulles airport resumed 1 May 2015, with four flights weekly.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 March 2021, Aer Lingus announced the launch of new long-haul routes to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York JFK</a> and <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Boston</a> from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a>, using its <a href="/wiki/A321LR" class="mw-redirect" title="A321LR">A321LR</a> airliners.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Change_of_CEO">Change of CEO</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Change of CEO">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 18 July 2014, Aer Lingus said it had "been agreed" between the company and Mueller that he would step down as CEO and director in May 2015. Mueller left to join Malaysia Airlines as part of its restructuring exercise.<sup id="cite_ref-Mueller_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mueller-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> On 16 February 2015 the company announced that the new CEO and director would be Stephen Kavanagh, beginning 1 March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> As of 1 January 2019, Sean Doyle became the new Aer Lingus CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="IAG_takeover_.282014.2F2015.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="IAG_takeover_(2014/2015)">IAG takeover (2014/2015)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: IAG takeover (2014/2015)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 14 December 2014, International Airlines Group (IAG) (owner of British Airways, Iberia and <a href="/wiki/Vueling" title="Vueling">Vueling</a>) launched a \xe2\x82\xac1bn takeover-bid (\xe2\x82\xac2.30 per-share) for Aer Lingus Group plc. The Aer Lingus Board rejected the offer on 16 December 2014, with Aer Lingus commenting that the offer was, "preliminary, highly conditional and non-binding." It was further noted, "The board has reviewed the proposal and believes that it fundamentally undervalues Aer Lingus and its attractive prospects.
