Accordingly, the proposal was rejected..."<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 9 January 2015, Aer Lingus rejected a second-bid from IAG, proposing a \xe2\x82\xac2.40 per-share takeover.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 January 2015, IAG launched a third bid for Aer Lingus, proposing a \xe2\x82\xac2.55 per-share takeover offer, totalling close to \xe2\x82\xac1.4bn.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 January 2015, Aer Lingus\' Board announced that "the financial terms of IAG\'s third proposal for the airline are at a level it is willing to recommend.", Aer Lingus said it noted, "IAG\'s intentions regarding the future of the company, in particular, that Aer Lingus would operate as a separate business with its own brand, management and operations."<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 26 May 2015, the Irish government agreed to the sale of its 25% shareholding to IAG, with a takeover now dependent on Ryanair\'s position on the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-irishtimes.com_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irishtimes.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 10 July 2015, Ryanair voted to sell its nearly 30% stake in the airline. The takeover was later approved by the EU and US regulators subject to IAG giving up five <a href="/wiki/Landing_slot" title="Landing slot">slot pairs</a> at <a href="/wiki/London_Gatwick_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Gatwick Airport">London Gatwick Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On 2 September 2015, IAG assumed control of Aer Lingus.<sup id="cite_ref-IAGShare_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IAGShare-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> On 17 September 2015, following completion of the acquisition by IAG, the company\'s shares were withdrawn from the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Stock Exchange">Irish Stock Exchange</a> and the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="COVID-19_.282020.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="COVID-19_(2020)">COVID-19 (2020)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: COVID-19 (2020)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_aviation" title="Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on aviation">Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on aviation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_tourism" title="Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on tourism">Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on tourism</a></div>\n<p>On 25 February 2020, Aer Lingus noted it had been advised by the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Ireland)" title="Department of Foreign Affairs (Ireland)">Department of Foreign Affairs</a> that travel restrictions were being placed on several <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a> towns within Italy\'s <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a> region as a result of an outbreak of <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">Coronavirus</a> there,<sup id="cite_ref-COVID-19_statement_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COVID-19_statement-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> however stated all flights would continue to operate,<sup id="cite_ref-COVID-19_statement_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COVID-19_statement-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> further advising all flights operated would continue to comply with guidelines locally from the <a href="/wiki/Health_Service_Executive" title="Health Service Executive">HSE</a> as well as from the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Safety_Agency" title="European Aviation Safety Agency">EASA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-COVID-19_statement_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COVID-19_statement-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EI-EIM@PEK_(20200330095829).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/EI-EIM%40PEK_%2820200330095829%29.jpg/220px-EI-EIM%40PEK_%2820200330095829%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/EI-EIM%40PEK_%2820200330095829%29.jpg/330px-EI-EIM%40PEK_%2820200330095829%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/EI-EIM%40PEK_%2820200330095829%29.jpg/440px-EI-EIM%40PEK_%2820200330095829%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5121" data-file-height="3414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EI-EIM@PEK_(20200330095829).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Aer Lingus A330-300 in Beijing, China during late March 2020 retrieving PPE for Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/Health_Service_Executive" title="Health Service Executive">HSE</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>On 28 February, Aer Lingus had been informed that a passenger had travelled with COVID-19 on a service from Milan-Linate to Dublin<sup id="cite_ref-NI_Covid_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NI_Covid-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> and that it was cooperating fully with the HSE and Department for Foreign Affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-COVID-19_statement_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COVID-19_statement-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Four Aer Lingus Cabin Crew were also placed into self-isolation from the flight in question.<sup id="cite_ref-NI_Covid_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NI_Covid-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The following day, Aer Lingus announced flight suspensions to Northern Italy,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> subsequently extending this on 10 March to all services to Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 March, Donald Trump, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>, announced a European travel ban which initially exempted Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> however was extended to cover Ireland the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Aer Lingus subsequently announced network-wide reductions<sup id="cite_ref-EI_cuts_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI_cuts-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> which eventually saw its network of flights reduced by 95%,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>  the airlines plan for its biggest summer schedule within its history was scuppered as a result of what became a <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">global pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> In a temporary measure, the airline confirmed it was cutting hours and salaries for all employees by 50%.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Later that month on 29 March, Aer Lingus flight EI9019 from <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> touched down at Dublin Airport carrying vital <a href="/wiki/Personal_protective_equipment" title="Personal protective equipment">PPE</a> for Ireland\'s health service workers, it marked the start of hundreds of flights the carrier was expected to operate to/from China on request of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of Ireland">Government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With just 5% of scheduled flights operating, it was announced on 1 May 2020 that Aer Lingus was seeking 900 job cuts.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The airline subsequently entered into talks with <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">Trade Unions</a> about changes to work practices and proposed job cuts,<sup id="cite_ref-EI_cuts_2_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI_cuts_2-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Aer Lingus CEO Sean Doyle commented that it would take years for the aviation industry to recover.<sup id="cite_ref-EI_cuts_2_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI_cuts_2-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Aer Lingus later confirmed it was seeking further temporary pay cuts and changes to work practices in a cost saving exercise,<sup id="cite_ref-EI_cuts_3_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI_cuts_3-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> advising that its 2021 schedule would be at least 20% lower than planned.<sup id="cite_ref-EI_cuts_3_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI_cuts_3-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Job cuts were confirmed later that month, those holding temporary contracts were made <a href="/wiki/Layoff" title="Layoff">redundant</a><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and Cabin Crew based in Shannon were informed that they would be temporarily laid off as the airline was not operating services from there.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 June, media reporting indicated broad acceptance of proposed measures based on a final draft document between Aer Lingus and Trade Unions,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> however the following day the union <a href="/wiki/F%C3%B3rsa" title="F\xc3\xb3rsa">F\xc3\xb3rsa</a> representing over 1,400 Aer Lingus Cabin Crew advised of its intention to <a href="/wiki/Ballot" title="Ballot">ballot</a> members.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The airline stated on 15 June, that if acceptance was not agreed by 6pm that evening, it would withdraw its offer and implement them <a href="/wiki/Unilateralism" title="Unilateralism">unilaterally</a> with a 70% cut to employees\xe2\x80\x99 wages excluding pilots.<sup id="cite_ref-EI_cuts_4_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI_cuts_4-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> As the deadline passed the airline initiated the action to implement the changes angering Trade Unions representing the majority of Aer Lingus employees.<sup id="cite_ref-EI_cuts_4_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EI_cuts_4-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> On 17 June, the airline agreed to allow a ballot for up to two weeks for its pilots for changes to work practices and recovery of salaries.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership_and_structure">Ownership and structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ownership and structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Aer Lingus was listed on the Irish and London Stock Exchanges, under ticker EIL1 on the Irish Stock Exchange and ticker AERL on the London Stock Exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> However it was delisted on 17 September 2015 following its majority acquisition by IAG.  Shareholdings (as of 2&#160;September&#160;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>) are:<sup id="cite_ref-IAGShare_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IAGShare-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background: #008374;"><span style="color:white">Shareholder</span>\n</th>\n<th style="background: #008374;"><span style="color:white">Shares</span>\n</th>\n<th style="background: #008374;"><span style="color:white">Interest</span>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a></td>\n<td align="right"></td>\n<td align="right">98.05%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Investor" title="Investor">Other investors</a></td>\n<td align="right"></td>\n<td align="right">1.95%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Total</b></td>\n<td align="right">534,040,090</td>\n<td align="right"><b>100.00%</b>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aer_Lingus_Cargo">Aer Lingus Cargo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Aer Lingus Cargo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Aer Lingus Cargo is the airline\'s cargo division. It uses reserved areas of passenger aircraft cargo-holds. Aer Lingus Cargo is available on all routes to the US from Dublin and <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon</a>. Cargo services are also offered on most European routes and some routes to the UK, the division subsequently rebranded as <a href="/wiki/IAG_Cargo" title="IAG Cargo">IAG Cargo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aer_Lingus_Regional">Aer Lingus Regional</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Aer Lingus Regional">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus_Regional" title="Aer Lingus Regional">Aer Lingus Regional</a></div>\n<p>Aer Lingus has a franchise agreement with Irish regional airline <a href="/wiki/Stobart_Air" title="Stobart Air">Stobart Air</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Aer_Arann" class="mw-redirect" title="Aer Arann">Aer Arann</a>), under which Stobart Air operates several routes under the <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus_Regional" title="Aer Lingus Regional">Aer Lingus Regional</a> brand, livery and flight code.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Stobart Air has not operated any flights under its own RE code since April 2012, and all its former routes have been transferred to Aer Lingus with flight numbers in the EI3XXX range.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_trends">Business trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Business trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Following its acquisition by IAG on 18 August 2015, separate Annual Reports are no longer published for Aer Lingus, however some data are shown separately within the IAG Annual Report.  Key available trends for Aer Lingus over recent years are shown below (as at year ending 31 December):\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em auto; text-align:center;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th end)\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>43\n</td>\n<td>44\n</td>\n<td>47\n</td>\n<td>50\n</td>\n<td>46\n</td>\n<td>47\n</td>\n<td>52\n</td>\n<th>56\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><br /><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><br /><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><br /><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_model">Business model</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Business model">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Aer Lingus adopted a "small frills" strategic approach \xe2\x80\x93 a hybrid between a traditional legacy airline and a <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carrier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bamber,_G.J.,_Gittell,_J.H.,_Kochan,_T.A._&amp;_von_Nordenflytch,_A._2009_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bamber,_G.J.,_Gittell,_J.H.,_Kochan,_T.A._&amp;_von_Nordenflytch,_A._2009-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The difference lies in the services offered on short-haul and long-haul flights with meals offered free on the latter only.\n</p><p>The new strategy required considerable negotiation with the unions, and a consensus was reached that lower costs and a reinvention of the airline were necessary for its survival. The union concessions that arose from the negotiations were detrimental to the airline\'s image however; by 2003 the wage freeze had been lifted and there were 3,800 voluntary redundancies with no forced layoffs. These factors contributed to the airline\'s reported profits in 2002, 2003 and 2005, with only a small loss recorded in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Bamber,_G.J.,_Gittell,_J.H.,_Kochan,_T.A._&amp;_von_Nordenflytch,_A._2009_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bamber,_G.J.,_Gittell,_J.H.,_Kochan,_T.A._&amp;_von_Nordenflytch,_A._2009-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Head_office">Head office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Head office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_Building,_Dublin_Airport,_County_Dublin,_Ireland_-_August_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_Building,_Dublin_Airport,_County_Dublin,_Ireland_-_August_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aer Lingus\' head office.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A320_Aer_Lingus_%22Retrojet%22_F-WWDV_EI-DVM,_MSN_4634.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A320_Aer_Lingus_%22Retrojet%22_F-WWDV_EI-DVM,_MSN_4634.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A320</a> in the retro livery at Toulouse\xe2\x80\x93Blagnac Airport in 2011 before delivery to the airline.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Self_check-in_at_Dublin_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Self_check-in_at_Dublin_Airport.jpg/220px-Self_check-in_at_Dublin_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Self_check-in_at_Dublin_Airport.jpg/330px-Self_check-in_at_Dublin_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Self_check-in_at_Dublin_Airport.jpg/440px-Self_check-in_at_Dublin_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2044" data-file-height="1410" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Self_check-in_at_Dublin_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Airport_check-in" title="Airport check-in">Self-check-in</a> machines of Aer Lingus at <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin Airport</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Aer Lingus head office is located on the grounds of Dublin Airport in <a href="/wiki/Fingal" title="Fingal">Fingal</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Dublin" title="County Dublin">County Dublin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Dublin Airport Authority (DAA) renovated an existing building to create Aer Lingus\'s headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The HOB Site,<sup id="cite_ref-SurrenderHOB_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SurrenderHOB-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> the 9.9-acre (4.0&#160;ha) former head office site includes the former head office building, the services annexe, the Iolar House,<sup id="cite_ref-HQSurrender_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HQSurrender-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> the Mock-Up Building, the ALSAA swimming pool, and various smaller structures and buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-SurrenderHOB_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SurrenderHOB-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The Head Office Building housed the corporate head office of Aer Lingus and its subsidiaries, and many administrative functions, employees, and car parking spaces, were located in this building. The Iolar House and Mock-Up Building housed training facilities for Aer Lingus crew and office space.<sup id="cite_ref-SurrenderHOB_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SurrenderHOB-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> This former head office is proximate to the former Ryanair head office. Brian Lavery of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> said in 2004 that the proximity, described by Lavery as "a few parking lots away," was "a symbol of just how close the competition is to home."<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Aer Lingus announced that it surrendered the lease on its head office building to the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Airport Authority">Dublin Airport Authority</a> and that it would move its employees to Hangar 6 and other buildings in the airline\'s property portfolio during the year of 2011. The airline said that its head office building, which was stated by the <i><a href="/wiki/International_Business_Times" title="International Business Times">International Business Times</a></i> to require refurbishing, was too large for the company\'s needs following the "Greenfield" cost reduction programme.<sup id="cite_ref-HQSurrender_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HQSurrender-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> On 8 November 2011 Aer Lingus signed the contract with the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Airport Authority">Dublin Airport Authority</a> for the surrender of the leasehold interest in the HOB Site. Aer Lingus would pay \xe2\x82\xac22.15 million and interest to the DAA, with \xe2\x82\xac10.55 million being paid over ten years in annual payments, with each being equal size. The payments will involve a 5% interest rate per annum.<sup id="cite_ref-SurrenderHOB_122-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SurrenderHOB-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The former HOB Site was redeveloped into Dublin Airport Central, with the Dublin Airport Authority planning to spend \xe2\x82\xac10 million. The former head office became One, Dublin Airport Central.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employee_relations">Employee relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Employee relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 30 May 2014, Aer Lingus <a href="/wiki/Flight_attendant" title="Flight attendant">cabin crew</a> staged a 24-hour <a href="/wiki/Strike_action" title="Strike action">strike</a> resulting in the cancellation of around 200 flights and the disruption of travel plans by up to 200,000 people. The workers were seeking changes to their <a href="/wiki/Schedule_(workplace)" title="Schedule (workplace)">rosters</a>, which the airline said that if implemented would mean the loss of 300 jobs in Ireland, which would have to be relocated to <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AerLingus_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AerLingus-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships">Sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sponsorships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 30 April 2015, it was announced that Aer Lingus would become the Official Airline of the <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Ireland national rugby union team">Irish Rugby Team</a>. On the same day, it was announced that one aircraft was to be renamed "Green Spirit" and wear a special livery for the Irish Rugby Team. Another aircraft would also be painted in the same livery.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Aer_Lingus_destinations" title="List of Aer Lingus destinations">List of Aer Lingus destinations</a></div>\n<p>As of April 2020, Aer Lingus flies to 93 destinations throughout <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>; including destinations in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Codeshare_agreements">Codeshare agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Codeshare agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Aer Lingus has <a href="/wiki/Codeshare_agreement" title="Codeshare agreement">codeshare agreements</a> with the following airlines:<sup id="cite_ref-CAPA_Aer_Lingus_profile_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAPA_Aer_Lingus_profile-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Fleet development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In January 2017, Aer Lingus announced its intention to finalize an order for seven <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320neo" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320neo">A321LR</a> twinjets to develop thinner transatlantic routes which cannot be operated profitably using A330s. As of November 2018, the airline has orders for fourteen A321LRs.<sup id="cite_ref-A321LR_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A321LR-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Air_Show" title="Paris Air Show">Paris Air Show</a> IAG agreed to purchase 14 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320neo_family" title="Airbus A320neo family">Airbus A321XLR</a> aircraft, 8 for delivery to <a href="/wiki/Iberia_(airline)" title="Iberia (airline)">Iberia</a> and 6 to Aer Lingus, with options for a further 14 of the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The first aircraft will be delivered in 2023 and replace their Boeing 757-200s.\nIn April 2020, Aer Lingus terminated their contract with the Irish airline <a href="/wiki/CityJet" title="CityJet">CityJet</a> which operated 2 <a href="/wiki/Avro_RJ" class="mw-redirect" title="Avro RJ">BAE Avro RJ85</a>\xe2\x80\x99s on behalf of the airline. The aircraft were primarily used for the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin</a> to <a href="/wiki/London_City_Airport" title="London City Airport">London-City</a> route.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_fleet">Historical fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Livery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 17 January 2019, Aer Lingus unveiled a new brand and livery. The refreshed brand includes a new typeface, refreshed shamrock and a new colour scheme. The new livery consists of a white fuselage and teal engines and tail. All aircraft are expected to be painted in the new livery by the end of 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In-flight_services">In-flight services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: In-flight services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From 2015 to 2016, Aer Lingus sold pre-packaged <a href="/wiki/Tayto_(Republic_of_Ireland)" title="Tayto (Republic of Ireland)">Tayto</a> sandwiches on board some of their flights.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, the company announced that it would offer a complimentary glass of wine or beer on transatlantic flights.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> That year the company also announced plans to offer free wifi to Smart Fare transatlantic economy customers.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, Aer Lingus introduced AerSpace, its premium economy class.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Frequent-flyer_programme">Frequent-flyer programme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Frequent-flyer programme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>AerClub is Aer Lingus\' frequent-flyer programme. It launched in November 2016, taking over from the airline\'s previous programme, Gold Circle. AerClub consists of four tiers: the entry-level Green, Silver, Platinum, and Concierge.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The club uses <a href="/wiki/Avios" class="mw-redirect" title="Avios">Avios</a> points as its member currency.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Memorial_to_the_Aer_Lingus_crash_of_January_1952_-_1784244.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Memorial_to_the_Aer_Lingus_crash_of_January_1952_-_1784244.jpg/220px-Memorial_to_the_Aer_Lingus_crash_of_January_1952_-_1784244.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Memorial_to_the_Aer_Lingus_crash_of_January_1952_-_1784244.jpg/330px-Memorial_to_the_Aer_Lingus_crash_of_January_1952_-_1784244.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Memorial_to_the_Aer_Lingus_crash_of_January_1952_-_1784244.jpg/440px-Memorial_to_the_Aer_Lingus_crash_of_January_1952_-_1784244.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="714" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Memorial_to_the_Aer_Lingus_crash_of_January_1952_-_1784244.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A memorial at the site of the January 1952 crash.</div></div></div>\n<p>Aer Lingus has a good safety record, with no crash fatalities in the past 50 years.\n</p><p>It has had 12 incidents, including six accidents which left aircraft written-off (of which three were fatal) and one hijacking.\n</p>\n<ul><li>On 10 January 1952, a <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">Douglas DC-3</a> (actually a civilianised ex-military Dakota) registered EI-AFL and named "St. Kevin" was en route from <a href="/wiki/RAF_Northolt" title="RAF Northolt">Northolt</a> to Dublin. It flew into a <a href="/wiki/Lee_wave" title="Lee wave">mountain wave</a> triggered by <a href="/wiki/Snowdon" title="Snowdon">Snowdon</a> and an area of extreme turbulence, then crashed in a peat bog near <a href="/wiki/Llyn_Gwynant" title="Llyn Gwynant">Llyn Gwynant</a> in <a href="/wiki/Snowdonia" title="Snowdonia">Snowdonia</a>, killing all 20 passengers and 3 crew. It was the company\'s first fatal accident.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 1 January 1953, a <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">Douglas DC-3</a> registered EI-ACF and named "St Kieran" made a forced landing near the town of <a href="/wiki/Spernall" title="Spernall">Spernall</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. Both engines failed after <a href="/wiki/Fuel_starvation" title="Fuel starvation">running out of fuel</a> while en route from <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> to <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>. All of the 25 passengers and crew survived. The aircraft was later written off.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 22 June 1967, a <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> registered EI-AOF on a pilot-training flight stalled and spun into the ground near <a href="/wiki/Ashbourne,_County_Meath" title="Ashbourne, County Meath">Ashbourne</a>, killing all three crew.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 21 September 1967, <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> EI-AKK flying from Dublin to Bristol scraped its wing on the runway and crashed on landing at the destination airport. All of the passengers and crew survived. The aircraft was later written off.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 24 March 1968, a <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> (registration: EI-AOM, named "St. Phelim") en route from <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a> to London crashed near <a href="/wiki/Tuskar_Rock,_Ireland" title="Tuskar Rock, Ireland">Tuskar Rock</a> in the waters off the southeast coast of Ireland. All 57 passengers and 4 crew perished. The crash is generally known as the <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus_Flight_712" title="Aer Lingus Flight 712">Tuskar Rock Air Disaster</a> in Ireland. Part of the aircraft\'s elevator spring tab was found some distance from the rest of the wreckage, suggesting that it had become detached at an earlier stage. However, the accident report reached no definitive conclusion about the cause of the crash but did not exclude the possibility that another aircraft or airborne object was involved. Following persistent rumours that the aircraft\'s demise was linked with nearby British military exercises, a review of the case files by the <a href="/wiki/Air_Accident_Investigation_Unit" title="Air Accident Investigation Unit">Air Accident Investigation Unit</a> took place in 1998. This review identified several maintenance and record-keeping failures and concluded that the original report failed to adequately examine alternative hypotheses not involving other aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> A subsequent investigation<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> concluded that the accident happened following a structural failure of the port tailplane, and ruled out the possibility that another aircraft was involved.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li>On 2 May 1981, <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus_Flight_164" title="Aer Lingus Flight 164">Aer Lingus Flight 164</a> from Dublin to London was hijacked and diverted to <a href="/wiki/Le_Touquet_%E2%80%93_C%C3%B4te_d%27Opale_Airport" title="Le Touquet \xe2\x80\x93 C\xc3\xb4te d&#39;Opale Airport">Le Touquet \xe2\x80\x93 C\xc3\xb4te d\'Opale Airport</a> in France. While authorities negotiated with the hijacker by radio in the cockpit, French special forces entered the rear of the aircraft and overpowered him. None of the passengers or crew were injured during the hijacking. The official record shows the reason as <i>One hijacker demanded to be taken to Iran. Plane stormed/hijacker arrested. Duration of the hijacking: less than 1 day.</i><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> while various media reports indicated that the man, Laurence Downey (a former <a href="/wiki/Trappists" title="Trappists">Trappist</a> monk), demanded that the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a> release the <a href="/wiki/Secret_of_Fatima#Third_secret" class="mw-redirect" title="Secret of Fatima">third secret of F\xc3\xa1tima</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 31 January 1986, Aer Lingus Flight 328, a <a href="/wiki/Short_360" title="Short 360">Short 360</a> registration EI-BEM on a flight from <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> to <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Airport" title="East Midlands Airport">East Midlands Airport</a>, struck power lines and crashed short of the runway. There were no fatalities but two passengers were injured in the accident.<sup id="cite_ref-aviation-safety.net_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aviation-safety.net-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Ireland" title="Transport in Ireland">Transport in Ireland</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aer_Lingus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: The two-word term <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text">aer loingeas</i></i> (with <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text">loingeas</i></i> in the nominative case) is not possible according to these rules.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFMulligan2017" class="citation news cs1">Mulligan, John (15 November 2017). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.independent.ie/business/irish/aer-lingus-has-no-plans-to-rejoin-airline-alliance-36320589.html">"Aer Lingus has \'no plans\' to rejoin airline alliance"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Irish_Independent" title="Irish Independent">Irish Independent</a></i><span class="reference-accessdate">.
